  { 
   "cell_type": "markdown", 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "source": [ 
    "The main database can be found [here](https://github.com/isadrtdinov/Solar-Activity/tree/master/data) in ***rgofull.txt***\n", 
    "\n", 
    "This file contains daily sunspot observations from 1874 to 1975. Each observation includes data about time of observation, group identifier, visible and corrected area, heliographic coordinates. The rules of storing data are written in ***rulesrgo.txt***\n", 
    "\n", 
    "It is possible to load the database directly from the file, but it is not adviced as it takes pretty much time (about 45-50 minutes, I don't know exactly why). Nevertheless, this can be done by the following function:" 
   ] 
  },

    "\n", 
    "rand_id = rand.choice(list(new_spots))\n", 
    "spot = new_spots[rand_id]\n", 
    "print(type(spot))\n", 
    "print('Printing states of spot #', rand_id, sep='')\n", 
    "print('Total states:', spot.lifetime, end='\\n\\n')\n", 
    "for state in spot.states:\n", 
    "    if state is None:\n", 
    "        print('The observation is missing (perhaps the group was invisible)', end='\\n\\n')\n", 
    "        continue\n", 
    "\n", 
    "    print(type(state))\n", 
    "    print('Observation time:', state.time)\n", 
    "    print('Corrected whole area:', state.wh_area)\n", 
    "    print('Carrington longitude:', state.carrington)\n", 
    "    print('Stonyhurst longitude:', state.stonyhurst)\n", 
    "    print('Latitude:', state.lat)\n",

   "cell_type": "markdown", 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "source": [ 
    "### Algorithm parameters" 
   ] 
  }, 
  { 
   "cell_type": "markdown", 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "source": [ 
    "The algorithm uses several macro-parameters. This section explains their meaning and illustrates methods to set them. Each parameter is a global variable that can be easily accessed.\n", 
    "\n", 
    "The parameters are:\n", 
    "- n_dim - a number of dimensions for the vector space (as spot histories are converted to vectors)\n", 
    "- n_neighbours - a number of nearest neighbours used for predictions\n", 
    "- n_clusters - a number of clusters for pre-processing (to speed up search of neighbours)\n", 
    "- min_area - minimal area for spot to be considered in measuring error, not used in predictions, only for error measuring (as small spots are hard to predict, the error becomes overestimated)\n", 
    "- decrease_rate - a rate of sudden decrease event\n", 
    "- decrease_prb - a probability of sudden decrease event\n", 
    "- disappear_area - minimal spot area for continuing lifetime prediction" 
   ] 
  }, 
  { 
   "cell_type": "markdown", 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "source": [ 
    "The params can be set using the following function\n", 
    "\n", 
    "**set_params**(new_*param_name*=**new_value**)\n", 
    "\n", 
    "Sets new values to mentioned parameters\n", 
    "\n", 
    "It is adviced to set needed values of parameters before calling any algorithm functions. It is not adviced to set parameters directly\n", 
    "\n", 
    "Example:" 
   ] 
  }, 
  { 
   "cell_type": "code", 
   "execution_count": 39, 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "outputs": [ 
    { 
     "name": "stdout", 
     "output_type": "stream", 
     "text": [ 
      "n_dim = 2\n", 
      "n_clusters = 20\n", 
      "disappear_area = 15.0\n", 
      "\n", 
      "n_dim = 4\n", 
      "n_neighbours = 3\n", 
      "decrease_rate = 2.5\n" 
     ] 
    } 
   ], 
   "source": [ 
    "sp.set_params(new_n_dim=2, new_n_clusters=20, new_disappear_area=15.0)\n", 
    "print('n_dim =', sp.n_dim)\n", 
    "print('n_clusters =', sp.n_clusters)\n", 
    "print('disappear_area =', sp.disappear_area, end='\\n\\n')\n", 
    "\n", 
    "sp.set_params(new_n_dim=4, new_n_neighbours=3, new_decrease_rate=2.5)\n", 
    "print('n_dim =', sp.n_dim)\n", 
    "print('n_neighbours =', sp.n_neighbours)\n", 
    "print('decrease_rate =', sp.decrease_rate)" 
   ] 
  },

   "cell_type": "markdown", 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "source": [ 
    "### Generating samples" 
   ] 
  }, 
  { 
   "cell_type": "markdown", 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "source": [ 
    "Now we can prepare the fitting sample for the algorithm. There is a function for this purpose:\n", 
    "\n", 
    "**clusterize_data**(*spots*)\n", 
    "\n", 
    "Prepares the fitting sample for the algorithm using *spots* database.\n", 
    "\n", 
    "Returns:\n", 
    "- *k_means* - sklearn cluster object\n", 
    "- *clusters* - clusterized fitting sample\n", 
    "- *sample* - examimation sample (for error measuring, does not intersect with the fitting sample)" 
   ] 
  }, 
  { 
   "cell_type": "code", 
   "execution_count": 46, 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "outputs": [], 
   "source": [ 
    "sp.set_params(new_n_dim=3, new_n_clusters=30)\n", 
    "k_means, clusters, sample = sp.clusterize_data(new_spots)" 
   ] 
  }, 
  { 
   "cell_type": "markdown", 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "source": [ 
    "### Predicting" 
   ] 
  }, 
  { 
   "cell_type": "markdown", 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "source": [ 
    "Now we are ready to predict spot areas. Let's start with a single spot.\n", 
    "\n", 
    "**generate_vector**(*spot*, *day*)\n", 
    "\n", 
    "Generates a vector from *spot* that area observed on *day* (counts from 0) becomes the last coordinate of the vector. Unknown spot areas are replaced by following day areas (a kind of const regression)\n", 
    "\n", 
    "**predict_area**(*spot_id*, *vec*, *mode*=**'mean'**, *k_means*=**None**, *clusters*=**None**, *descrease*=**None**)\n", 
    "\n", 
    "Returns an area prediction for vector *vec*\n", 
    "\n", 
    "Params:\n", 
    "- *spot_id*: spot identifier, is passed to avoid the spot predicting itself\n", 
    "- *mode*: **'mean'** - prediction is a mean area of neighbours, **'weighted'** - weighted (upon distances) area of neighbours (actually does not work better than 'mean') or **'naive'** - decreased last known area (last coordinate of *vec*)\n", 
    "- *k_means*, *clusters* - fitting sample (see above), for **'mean'** and **'weighted'** modes only\n", 
    "- *decrease* - decrease rate, for **'naive'** mode only (e.g. decrease=0.9 means that area is decreased by 10%)" 
   ] 
  }, 
  { 
   "cell_type": "code", 
   "execution_count": 137, 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "outputs": [ 
    { 
     "name": "stdout", 
     "output_type": "stream", 
     "text": [ 
      "Real area: 1347.0\n", 
      "Mean prediction: 1274.3333333333333\n", 
      "Weighted prediction: 1236.0274964965838\n", 
      "Naive prediction: 1157.1\n" 
     ] 
    } 
   ], 
   "source": [ 
    "sp.set_params(new_n_neighbours=3)\n", 
    "rand_id = None\n", 
    "spot = None\n", 
    "while True:\n", 
    "    rand_id = rand.choice(list(new_spots))\n", 
    "    spot = new_spots[rand_id]\n", 
    "    if spot.lifetime <= sp.n_dim:\n", 
    "        continue\n", 
    "    rand_day = rand.randrange(sp.n_dim - 1, spot.lifetime - 1)\n", 
    "    if spot.states[rand_day] is None or spot.states[rand_day + 1] is None:\n", 
    "        continue\n", 
    "    break\n", 
    "vec = sp.generate_vector(spot, rand_day)\n", 
    "print('Real area:', spot.states[rand_day + 1].wh_area)\n", 
    "print('Mean prediction:', sp.predict_area(rand_id, vec, mode='mean', k_means=k_means, clusters=clusters))\n", 
    "print('Weighted prediction:', sp.predict_area(rand_id, vec, mode='weighted', k_means=k_means, clusters=clusters))\n", 
    "print('Naive prediction:', sp.predict_area(rand_id, vec, mode='naive', decrease=0.95))" 
   ] 
  }, 
  { 
   "cell_type": "markdown", 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "source": [ 
    "We can also predict sample areas:\n", 
    "\n", 
    "**predict_sample**(*sample*, *mode*=**'mean'**, *k_means*=**None**, *clusters*=**None**, *decrease*=**None**)\n", 
    "\n", 
    "Predicts *sample* areas. The rest parameters are the same as above\n", 
    "\n", 
    "Predicting such sample takes about 15-20 minutes" 
   ] 
  }, 
  { 
   "cell_type": "code", 
   "execution_count": 140, 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "outputs": [], 
   "source": [ 
    "prediction = sp.predict_sample(sample, mode='mean', k_means=k_means, clusters=clusters)" 
   ] 
  }, 
  { 
   "cell_type": "markdown", 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "source": [ 
    "### Measuring errors" 
   ] 
  }, 
  { 
   "cell_type": "markdown", 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "source": [ 
    "The library contains a simple function to calculate relative errors of the prediction.\n", 
    "\n", 
    "**error_distribution**(*sample*, *prediction*)\n", 
    "\n", 
    "Returns a list of errors for *sample* with *predictions*. The errors are calculated with the following formula:\n", 
    "\n", 
    "$ \\epsilon = \\frac {S_{pr} - S_*} {S_*}$, where $ S_* $ is real area, $ S_{pr} $ is predicted area\n", 
    "\n", 
    "Note that only spots with $ S_* > $ *min_area* are considered" 
   ] 
  }, 
  { 
   "cell_type": "code", 
   "execution_count": 145, 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "outputs": [], 
   "source": [ 
    "import matplotlib.pyplot as plt\n", 
    "import numpy as np\n", 
    "%matplotlib inline" 
   ] 
  }, 
  { 
   "cell_type": "code", 
   "execution_count": 143, 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "outputs": [], 
   "source": [ 
    "errors = sp.error_distribution(sample, prediction)" 
   ] 
  }, 
  { 
   "cell_type": "code", 
   "execution_count": 148, 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "outputs": [ 
    {

    "### Predicting histories" 
   ] 
  }, 
  { 
   "cell_type": "markdown", 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "source": [ 
    "After discussing single-day prediction we can proceed to history predicting. For a single spot there is a following function:\n", 
    "\n", 
    "**life_prediction**(*spot*, *mode*=**'mean'**, *k_means*=**None**, *clusters*=**None**, *decrease*=**None**, *sudden_decrease*=**False**)\n", 
    "\n", 
    "Returns a new **Sunspot** class exemplar with corrected history. All parameters are the same as above, *sudden_decrease* allows sudden decrease event\n", 
    "\n", 
    "All missing states are also filled with the use of the algorithm. Spot history is enlonged iff it ends on the right edge of the solar hemisphere (stonyhurst longitude is $ > 90 - 2 * \\frac {180} {14} = 64.285 $ degrees, which matches 2 days of observation).\n", 
    "\n", 
    "Note that the algorithm does not predict coordinate change, so the new states are initialized with a last known value. It is also not precise enough on small spots" 
   ] 
  }, 
  { 
   "cell_type": "code",

    "sp.set_params(new_decrease_rate=1 / 3, new_decrease_prb=1 / 7, new_disappear_area=15.0)" 
   ]

    "def example():\n", 
    "    rand_id = rand.choice(list(new_spots))\n", 
    "    spot = new_spots[rand_id]\n", 
    "    for state in spot.states:\n", 
    "        if state is None:\n", 
    "            print(None)\n", 
    "            continue\n", 
    "        print('area:', state.wh_area, 'longitude:', '%.3f' % state.stonyhurst, 'simulated:', state.simulated)\n", 
    "\n", 
    "    print()\n", 
    "    new_spot = sp.life_prediction(spot, mode='mean', k_means=k_means, clusters=clusters, sudden_decrease=True)\n", 
    "\n", 
    "    for state in new_spot.states:\n", 
    "        if state is None:\n", 
    "            print(None)\n", 
    "            continue\n", 
    "        print('area:', state.wh_area, 'longitude:', '%.3f' % state.stonyhurst, 'simulated:', state.simulated)" 
   ]

   "cell_type": "markdown", 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "source": [ 
    "### Illustrating lifetime distribution" 
   ] 
  }, 
  { 
   "cell_type": "markdown", 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "source": [ 
    "The library provides a function that calculates lifetime distribution through the database:\n", 
    "\n", 
    "**lifetime_distribution**(*spots*, *max_lifetime*=**100**, *center_spots*=**False**, *center_rate*=**2 / 3**, *eps*=**0.001**)\n", 
    "\n", 
    "Returns a list of lifetime distribution (1 day - list\\[0\\], 2 days - \\[1\\])\n", 
    "\n", 
    "Params:\n", 
    "- *spots* - the database to analyse (Python dict)\n", 
    "- *max_lifetime* - maximal allowed lifetime\n", 
    "- *center_spots* - if is set **True** than are consider only those spots, which were born in the center of the solat hemisphere (filters spots that come from the left edge)\n", 
    "- *center_rate* - limits the central part of the solar hemisphere (e.g. **2 / 3** corresponds to \\[-60, 60\\] degrees)\n", 
    "- *eps* - a cutoff to get rid of the tail (to drop **0** values)" 
   ] 
  }, 
  { 
   "cell_type": "markdown", 
   "metadata": {}, 
   "source": [ 
    "One more useful function:\n", 
    "\n", 
    "**exponent_approximation**(*data, X, A ,B*)\n", 
    "\n", 
    "Calculates best MSE exponent approximation $ e ^ {ax + b}$\n", 
    "\n", 
    "Params:\n", 
    "- *data*: data values\n", 
    "- *X*: data arguments\n", 
    "- *A*: range for a parameter\n", 
    "- *B*: range for b parameter" 
   ] 
  },
